                    <tr style="background-color: #FFF;"><td style="border-top:2px solid #D3D3D3; font-size:10pt;"><div style="padding-top:5px; padding-bottom:5px; padding-left:5px; padding-right:5px;"><b><a href="http://www.rotowire.com/users/ad_jump.asp?id=688&playerid=8807" style="text-decoration:none;">RotoWire News</a>:</b> Feldman (7-6) gave up four runs on five hits and a walk while striking out six over five innings in Wednesday's 5-3 loss to the Rockies.                 <tr style="background-color: #FFF;"><td style="border-top:2px solid #D3D3D3; vertical-align:top; padding-bottom:4px; padding-left:5px;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:13pt"><span class="m_date">6/15/2017</span> - <a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/fantasy/velocity-decliners-from-the-seasons-start/">Velocity Decliners From the Season's Start</a><span class="m_comments"> by </span><span class="m_author"><a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/fantasy/index.php?author=7554">Jeff Zimmerman (RotoGraphs)</a></span><span class="m_comments">&nbsp;<a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/fantasy/velocity-decliners-from-the-seasons-start/#comments"><img src="images/commentslink.gif" border="0px" />10</a></span><br /><span class="m_date">3/15/2016</span> - <a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/fantasy/stream-stream-stream-the-return-of-2xsp-for-2015-4-13-19/">Stream, Stream, Stream: The Return of #2xSP for 20&raquo;</a><span class="m_comments"> by </span><span class="m_author"><a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/fantasy/index.php?author=26727">Brandon Warne (RotoGraphs)</a></span><span class="m_comments">&nbsp;<a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/fantasy/stream-stream-stream-the-return-of-2xsp-for-2015-4-13-19/#comments"><img src="images/commentslink.gif" border="0px" />12</a></span><br /><span class="m_date">10/24/2014</span> - <a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/blogs/scott-feldman-on-scuffed-balls-lopsided-balls-and-pitching-up/">Scott Feldman on Scuffed Balls, Lopsided Balls, an&raquo;</a><span class="m_comments"> by </span><span class="m_author"><a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/blogs/index.php?author=25048">David Laurila (FanGraphs)</a></span><span class="m_comments">&nbsp;<a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/blogs/scott-feldman-on-scuffed-balls-lopsided-balls-and-pitching-up/#comments"><img src="images/commentslink.gif" border="0px" />5</a></span><br /></div></td></tr>

                <tr id="so1" style="background-color: #FFF;"><td colspan="5" style="border-top:2px solid #D3D3D3; padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="width:100%; font-size:10pt"><center>Profiles:&nbsp;&nbsp;<a id="soa2" href="javascript:showMoreSO();">2010</a>&nbsp;&nbsp;<a id="soa3" href="javascript:showMoreSO2011();">2011</a>&nbsp;&nbsp;<a id="soa4" href="javascript:showMoreSO2012();">2012</a>&nbsp;&nbsp;<a id="soa5" href="javascript:showMoreSO2013();">2013</a>&nbsp;&nbsp;<a id="soa6" href="javascript:showMoreSO2014();">2014</a>&nbsp;&nbsp;<a id="soa7" href="javascript:showMoreSO2015();">2015</a>&nbsp;&nbsp;<a id="soa8" href="javascript:showMoreSO2016();">2016</a>&nbsp;&nbsp;(Click Year to Expand / <a href="javascript:hideSO('so1');">Close</a>)</center></div></td></tr>
                <tr id="so2" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Year in Review: </b>There's something unbelievably compelling about an individual who succeeds not by means of sheer ability but through some combination of hard work and/or ingenuity. You want proof? How about every Hollywood film? Or, in the case of baseball, how about Scott Feldman? Of course, it's a slight misnomer to say that someone who's 6'5" and throws a ball 90 mph lacks sheer ability; still, it takes more than that to succeed at the Major League level. In the past several seasons, Feldman has gone from mildly effective, ground-balling reliever to slightly less effective innings-eater to borderline legitimate Cy Young candidate. The last of those developments is almost wholly attributable to the success of Feldman's cut fastball. The cutter, which Feldman didn't even throw as late as 2007, was worth 25.9 runs above average in 2009 per FanGraphs’ Pitch Value leader board – the fifth most valuable pitch in the league by that measure.<br /><br /><b>The Year Ahead: </b>Of course, the most striking thing about Feldman's 2009 campaign is his record: 17-8. That's certainly what fueled talk about his Cy Young candidacy as the season entered its final month. After blanking Cleveland on Sept. 9, he was 16-4; after beating the Angels 10 days later, he was 17-5. Unfortunately, his last three starts (and decisions) were all losses. Doubly unfortunate, Feldman doesn't really have the make-up of a 20- or even a 17-win pitcher. According to Baseball Prospectus, a pitcher of Feldman's description would typically have finished 13.3-8.4 with league average run support. Likewise, ZiPS sees Feldman as a 13-8 pitcher in 2010. When you consider that he'll have a hard time breaking the 100-strikeout barrier, and will probably also see some regression in batting average against (and thus, WHIP), it's hard to view Feldman as anything better than a middle-round pick.  (Carson Cistulli)</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
                <tr id="so3" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>After a fairly strong showing in 2009, the Rangers signed Scott Feldman to an extension. Immediately thereafter he reverted to being the player he was prior to 2009. Feldman certainly provided value to fantasy owners in 2009, with 17 wins, a 4.08 ERA, and a 1.28 WHIP. Those who were thinking repeat in 2010 were met with a player they likely cut by May. Feldman heads into 2011 as the likely odd man out in the Rangers rotation. They have enough young arms that using Feldman just doesn't make sense. Chances are he'll make a few spot starts between bullpen outings, but he's not going to provide much fantasy value -- he doesn't rack up the strikeouts, allows a lot of hits, and has problems keeping his ERA under 5.00. He can fill in for an emergency situation, but there's probably someone better. (Joe Pawlikowski)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Feldman had a relatively strong 2009 and started the 2010 season in the Rangers rotation, but after a poor season he likely won't have much of a chance in 2011. Unless the Rangers face injury or their younger starters don't work out, he won't be a factor.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
                <tr id="so4" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Feldman pitched pretty well out of the bullpen last season, but he doesn't miss bats and is stuck in a great hitters' park. Unless he plans on reverting to 2009 form, don't bother. (Mike Axisa)</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
                <tr id="so5" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>A move from Texas to Chicago should be a fortuitous one for Feldman's fantasy prospects, but under the surface it's a bit more ambiguous than it originally seems. For one, Feldman has never particularly suffered from Texas's home run-inducing ways -- he's only allowed two more home runs outside of Arlington (only 13 more innings out of 727 total) and his batting average on balls in play allowed is 11 points higher on the road as well. At least the league change is a clear help. If Feldman makes the rotation, his solid control is his best asset, but he's tougher to bet on in shallow leagues due to middling strikeout numbers (5.4 strikeouts per nine career, topping out at 7.0 K/9 in 2012). The new league should gift him a few strikeouts and make him a passable mixed leaguer. (Jack Moore)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>It isn't clear an exodus from Texas helps Feldman as much as it would other pitchers. Still, going to the National League will help if he can earn a rotation spot.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
                <tr id="so6" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Feldman has worked at least 180 innings just twice in the past five seasons. He is primarily a ground-ball pitcher which allows him to limit his home runs, and that will be put to the test as his home park is now Minute Maid Park. He has a below-league average strikeout rate, and since he does not miss many bats, his success is predicated on how his batting average on balls in play behaves. The issue there is the Saberhagenmetrics ((c) Razzball) he has with that stat. In even-numbered seasons since 2008, his BABIP has been .284, .327, and .318. In odd-numbered seasons, it has been .273, .239, and .258. His WHIP in those even-numbered seasons: 1.43, 1.60, and 1.38. In odd-numbered years, it has been 1.28, 1.09, and 1.18.With 2014 being an even-numbered season, that may be a problem, especially with the Astros infield defense outside of Matt Dominguez. The run support in Houston is not likely to be there, which makes him a reserve pick in mixed leagues and a risky late-round pick in AL-only leagues. The strikeouts should be there, but everything else is a risk. (Jason Collette)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>The run support in Houston is not likely to be there, which makes him a reserve pick in mixed leagues and a risky late round pick in AL-Only leagues. The strikeouts should be there, but everything else is a risk.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
                <tr id="so7" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Scott Feldman does not strike out enough hitters to ensure value for your fantasy rosters. In fact, for pitchers with more than 90 innings pitched, Feldman had the sixth-worst strikeout rate in baseball last year. A top-60 walk rate and an extensive enough repertoire enables Feldman to have ERAs less than 3.90. Somehow he's managed lower batting average on balls in play rates thus far in his career including a .258 in 2013. Luck and defense exacerbates the effect, but his extensive repertoire and command prevents damage. With that said, all of his pitches are below average from a swinging-strike standpoint. If we use 100 pitches as a qualifier, his cutter had the fifth worst rate and his changeup had the 12th-worst rate. This is even sadder when we consider that changeups have the <a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/fantasy/swinging-strike-benchmarks-for-pitch-types/">highest league SwStr%</a>. (<a href="https://twitter.com/RotoBanter">Dan Schwartz</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>If your league somehow omits any categories related to the strikeout, Feldman could be of value to you, otherwise his peripherals are not valuable enough to make his lack of strikeouts palatable.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
                <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Scott Feldman doesn't strike many batters out because he doesn't throw hard and doesn't miss bats. He does still manage to keep a very respectable batting average on balls in play, as he has throughout most of his career. Feldman has been known to have fairly good command, which has benefited him on the field, but doesn't really translate all that well to a fantasy roster. He still keeps an ERA under 4.00, so there's something to be said there, if the thing being said is "yeah, so what?" He dealt with some injuries in 2015, and is a prime candidate to get squeezed out of some starts should the Astros understandably elect to go (and stay) with some pitchers from their large stable of prospects. (David Temple)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>If your fantasy league counts Veteran Leadership as a category, Feldman might be worth a flyer. If, instead, it is based off of most other kinds of pitching stats, it's best to walk away.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
                
            </table>
        </td>
        <td style="width: 302px; height: 250px; vertical-align: top;">
            <div class="catchall300" style='width:300px; overflow:hidden;float:right;'><!-- RoS_300x250 --> <div id ='div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13' style='width:300px; height:250px; overflow:hidden;'><script type='text/javascript'>if ($('#div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13').is(':visible')) {googletag.cmd.push(function () { googletag.display('div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13'); });}</script></div></div>

        </td>
    </tr>
</table>

    function setAverage(t) {
        var elements;
        var browserCheck = (document.all) ? 1 : 0;
        if (t == '*') {
            elements = (ie) ? document.all : document.getElementsByTagName('*');
        } else {
            elements = document.getElementsByTagName(t);
        }
        for (var i = 0; i < elements.length; i++) {
            var node = elements.item(i);
            var vis = elements.item(i).style;
            for (var j = 0; j < node.attributes.length; j++) {
                if (node.attributes.item(j).nodeName == 'class') {
                    if (node.attributes.item(j).nodeValue == 'rgRow grid_average') {


                        if (browserCheck > 0) {

                            if (vis.display == undefined) {
                                vis.dispaly = 'block';
                            }
                            else {
                                if (vis.display == 'block') { vis.display = 'none'; } else { vis.display = 'block'; }
                            }

                        }

                        else {

                            if (vis.display == undefined) {
                                vis.dispaly = 'table-row';
                            }
                            else {
                                if (vis.display == 'table-row') { vis.display = 'none'; } else { vis.display = 'table-row'; }
                            }

                        }

                    }
                }
            }
        }
    }

    function setPart(t) {
        var elements;
        var browserCheck = (document.all) ? 1 : 0;
        if (t == '*') {
            elements = (ie) ? document.all : document.getElementsByTagName('*');

        for (var i = 0; i < elements.length; i++) {

            for (var j = 0; j < node.attributes.length; j++) {

    // Create the tooltips only on document load
    $(document).ready(function () {
        // Make sure to only match links to wikipedia with a rel tag
        $('a[tipgloss]').each(function () {
            // We make use of the .each() loop to gain access to each element via the "this" keyword...
            $(this).qtip(
		{
		    content: {
		        // Set the text to an image HTML string with the correct src URL to the loading image you want to use
		        text: " ",
		        ajax: {
		            url: $(this).attr('tipgloss') // Use the rel attribute of each element for the url to load
		        }
		    },
		    position: {
		        viewport: $(window),
		        at: "top center",
		        my: "bottom center",
		        effect: false
		    },
		    show: {
		        event: "click mouseenter",
		        solo: true // Only show one tooltip at a time
		    },
		    hide: {
		        event: "click mouseleave",
		        delay: 1000,
		        fixed: true
		    },
		    style: {
		        classes: "qtip-light"
		    }
		})

            // Make sure it doesn't follow the link when we click it
        });
    });
